Eggeling
  1. There is a reddish-white (he-goat as the victim) for the A┼Ыvins 3, for the A┼Ыvins are reddish-white. There is an ewe with teats in the dewlap 4 for Sarasvat─л; and a bull he seizes for Indra Sutr─Бman (the good protector) 5. Difficult to obtain are beasts with such perfections; if he cannot obtain any

with such perfections, they may slaughter only goats, for they are easier to cook. And if they seize only goats, that for the A┼Ыvins is a red one. Then as to why he performs this sacrifice.

Eggeling
  1. Indra thought within himself: ‘There now, they are excluding me from Soma!’ and even uninvited he consumed what pure (Soma) there was in the tub, as the stronger (would consume the food) of the weaker. But it hurt him: it flowed in all directions from (the openings of) his vital airs; only from his mouth it did not flow. Hence there was an atonement; but had it flown also from his mouth, then indeed there would have been no atonement.

Eggeling
  1. For there are four castes, the Br─Бhmaс╣Зa, the R─Бjanya, the Vai┼Ыya, and the ┼Ъ┼лdra; but there is not one of them that vomits Soma; but were there any one of them, then indeed there would be atonement.

Eggeling
  1. From what flowed from the nose a lion sprang; and from what flowed from the ears a wolf sprang; and from what flowed from the lower opening wild beasts sprang, with the tiger as their foremost; and what flowed from the upper opening that was the foaming spirit (parisrut). And thrice he spit out: thence were produced the (fruits called) ‘kuvala, karkandhu, or badara 9.’ He (Indra) became emptied out of everything, for Soma is everything.

  1. Let him also cure by this (ceremony) one purged by Soma;–he whom Soma purges is indeed emptied out of everything, for Soma is everything. Eggeling
  1. On (the meat-portions of) those victims he throws hairs of a lion, hairs of a wolf, and hairs of a tiger, for that was what sprang therefrom, when Soma flowed right through him. He now supplies

Eggeling
  1. But let him not do it so; for he who throws them on the (portions of) the victims, urges the animals on from behind with a clawed (prickly) fire-brand. Eggeling
  1. They take up two fires; on the northern altar 13 (they lay down) the northern (fire), and on a raised (mound) the southern one, thinking, ‘Lest we should offer together the Soma-libations, and the Sur─Б (liquor) -libations:’ therefore they take up two fires, and on the northern altar (they lay down) the northern (fire), and on a raised (mound) the southern one. And when he proceeds with the omenta, then he proceeds with that spirituous liquor.

Eggeling
  1. He purifies it with stalks of Darbha-grass, thinking, ‘Let it be pure,’–with (V─Бj. S. X, 31), ‘The inviting 14 Soma, purified by the purifying

(strainer), has overflown backwards, Indra’s mated friend.’ He then pours in flour of ‘kuvala, karkandhu, and badara’ berries, for when he (Indra) spit out thrice, that was what was produced therefrom: therewith he now supplies him and makes him whole,–therefore he pours in that (flour).

Eggeling
  1. He then draws either one or three cups 16,–but only one should be drawn, for there is one puroruc-formula, one invitatory prayer, and one offering prayer; therefore only one (cup) should be drawn.

реирек

рдореВрд▓рдореН - Weber

рдореВрд▓рдореН - рд╡рд┐рд╕реНрд╡рд░рдореН

рд╕ рдЧреГрд╣реНрдгрд╛рддрд┐- “рдХреБрд╡рд┐рджрдЩреНрдЧ рдпрд╡рдордиреНрддреЛ рдпрд╡рдВ рдЪрд┐рджреН рдпрдерд╛ рджрд╛рдиреНрддреНрдпрдиреБрдкреВрд░реНрд╡рдВ рд╡рд┐рдпреВрдп ред рдЗрд╣реЗрд╣реИрд╖рд╛рдВ рдХреГрдгреБрд╣рд┐ рднреЛрдЬрдирд╛рдирд┐ рдпреЗ рдмрд░реНрд╣рд┐рд╖реЛ рдирдордЙрдХреНрддрд┐рдВ рдпрдЬрдиреНрддрд┐ ред рдЙрдкрдпрд╛рдордЧреГрд╣реАрддреЛ рд╜рд╕реНрдпрд╢реНрд╡рд┐рднреНрдпрд╛рдВ рддреНрд╡рд╛, рд╕рд░рд╕реНрд╡рддреНрдпреИ рддреНрд╡рд╛, рдЗрдиреНрджреНрд░рд╛рдп рддреНрд╡рд╛ рд╕реБрддреНрд░рд╛рдореНрдгреЗ”- (рд╡рд╛. рд╕рдВ. резреж ред рейреи ред) рдЗрддрд┐ ред рдпрджреНрдпреБ рддреНрд░реАрдиреН рдЧреГрд╣реНрдгреАрдпрд╛рджреН рдПрддрдпреИрд╡ рдЧреГрд╣реНрдгреАрдпрд╛рддреН ред рдЙрдкрдпрд╛рдореИрд╕реНрддреБ рддрд░реНрд╣рд┐ рдирд╛рдирд╛ рдЧреГрд╣реНрдгреАрдпрд╛рджреН ред рдЕрдерд╛рд╣- рдЕрд╢реНрд╡рд┐рднреНрдпрд╛рдВ рд╕рд░рд╕реНрд╡рддреНрдпрд╛ рд╜рдЗрдиреНрджреНрд░рд╛рдп рд╕реБрддреНрд░рд╛рдореНрдгреЗ рд╜рдиреБрдмреНрд░реВрд╣реАрддрд┐ рее реирек рее

Eggeling
  1. He draws it with (V─Бj. S. X, 32), ‘Yea, even as the owners of barley cut their barley, spreading it asunder in due order, so hither, hither, bring thou the nourishments of them that offer up the devotional invocation of the Barhis 18!–Thou art taken with a support–thee for the A┼Ыvins, thee for Sarasvat─л, thee for Indra, the good protector!’ And if he draw three (cups), let him draw them with that same (verse); but let him in that case draw them with separate ‘supports 19.’ He then says, ‘Recite the

invitatory prayer to the A┼Ыvins, to Sarasvat─л, and to Indra Sutr─Бman!’

Eggeling
  1. He recites (V─Бj. S. X, 33; R╠еk S. X, 131, 4), ‘Ye, O A┼Ыvins, lords of splendour, having quaffed the cheering (Soma) together with Namuci, the ─Аsura, helped Indra in his deeds!’ Having called for the ┼Ъraushaс╣н, he says, ‘Pronounce the offering prayer to the A┼Ыvins, to Sarasvat─л, and to Indra Sutr─Бman!’

Eggeling
  1. He prays (V─Бj. S. X, 34; R╠еk S. X, 131, 5), ‘As the parents (stand by) their son, so the two A┼Ыvins have stood by thee, O Indra, with wise plans and wonderful deeds; when thou quaffedst the cheering (Soma), Sarasvat─л cured thee, O Lord, by her services.’ Twice the Hotr╠е utters the Vashaс╣н, twice the Adhvaryu offers and fetches drink. And if he draw three (cups of liquor), then after the offering of that one the other two are offered.

Eggeling
  1. Now there is a pitcher perforated either with a hundred, or with nine, holes. If it is one with a hundred holes,–man lives up to a hundred (years), and has a hundred energies, and a hundred powers: therefore it is perforated with a hundred holes. And if with nine holes,–there are in man those nine vital airs: therefore it is perforated with nine holes.

Eggeling
  1. This (pitcher), hung up by a sling, they hold just over the ─Аhavan─лya 25. He pours into it what spirituous liquor has been left over, and whilst it is

trickling through, he stands by worshipping with the three verses 26 of the Pitaraс╕е Somavantaс╕е (the Fathers accompanied by Soma), with three verses of the Pitaro Barishadaс╕е (the Fathers seated on the barhis), and with three verses of the Pitaro Agnishv─Бtt─Бс╕е (the Fathers consumed by the fire). And as to why he thus stands by worshipping,–when Soma flowed through Indra, what part of it then went to the Fathers–there being three kinds of Fathers–therewith he now supplies him and makes him whole: therefore he thus stands by worshipping.

Eggeling
  1. Let him, however, not do it in this way; for verily whosoever departs from the path of the sacrifice stumbles, and he who does this indeed departs from the path of the sacrifice. Hence at the very time when they proceed with the omenta of those victims, let them then proceed also with those (three) oblations, and let him not then prepare a two-kap─Бla cake for the A┼Ыvins.

рдЗрддрд┐ рд╢реНрд░реАрд╕рд╛рдпрдгрд╛рдЪрд╛рд░реНрдпрд╡рд┐рд░рдЪрд┐рддреЗ рдорд╛рдзрд╡реАрдпреЗ рд╡реЗрджрд╛рд░реНрдердкреНрд░рдХрд╛рд╢реЗ рдорд╛рдзреНрдпрдиреНрджрд┐рдиреАрдпрд╢рддрдкрдердмреНрд░рд╛рд╣реНрдордгрднрд╛рд╖реНрдпреЗ рдкрдЮреНрдЪрдордХрд╛рдгреНрдбреЗ рдкрдЮреНрдЪрдорд╛ рд╜рдзреНрдпрд╛рдпреЗ рдЪрддреБрд░реНрдердВ рдмреНрд░рд╛рд╣реНрдордгрдореН рее рел ред рел ред рек рее

Eggeling
  1. A castrated bull is the sacrificial fee for this

(sacrifice);–the castrated bull is neither female nor male; for being a male it is not a female, and being a female (unmanned) it is not a male: therefore a castrated bull is the fee. Or a draught-mare;–the draught-mare is neither male nor female; for in that it pulls the cart it is not a female; and being a female, it is not a male: therefore a draught-mare (may be) the fee.

  1. рд╢реБрд╢реНрд░с│Шрдпрддрд░рд╛ A. ↩︎

  2. рддреНрд░рд┐рдкрд╢реБрдГ рдкрд╢реБрдмрдВрдзрд╢реНрдЪрддреБрд░реНрдереНрдпрд╛рдореН ред рдХрд╛реж рд╢реНрд░реМреж рд╕реВреж резрел ред реиренрей ред ↩︎

  3. 129:1 The last three Soma-sacrifices of the Inauguration-ceremony are not even alluded to by the author, their performance involving no features different from those of the normal Soma-sacrifice. The Vyushс╣нi-dvir─Бtra, or ’two nightsтАЩ ceremony of the dawn,’ consists of an Agnishс╣нoma and an Atir─Бtra Soma-sacrifice, to be performed a month after the Ke┼Ыavapan─лya (or, according to Taitt. Br. I, 8, 10, a fortnight after, viz. on the new-moon, and the first day of the light fortnight respectively). Finally, the Kshatra-dhr╠еti, or ‘wielding of the ruling-power,’ an Agnishс╣нoma, is performed a month later, or on the full-moon of ┼Ъr─Бvaс╣Зa (about 1 August). Some authorities, however, allow the Soma-sacrifices of the Inauguration-ceremony to conclude with the Ke┼Ыavapan─лya Atir─Бtra (K─Бty. ┼Ъr. XV, 9, 26), perhaps for the very reason that no mention is made in the Br─Бhmaс╣Зa of the remaining three Soma-days. The final Soma-sacrifice is followed, in the succeeding fortnight of the waxing moon, by the performance of the Sautr─Бmaс╣З─л, some peculiar features of which the author now proceeds to consider. This ceremony (one of the objects of which is the expiation of any excess committed in the consumption of Soma-juice) is considered in the sacrificial system as the last of the seven forms of Haviryaj├▒a; being a combination of the ishс╣нi with the animal sacrifice. As this ceremony is also performed after the Agnicayana, or construction of the fire-altar, it is more fully dealt with by the author later on (K─Бс╣Зс╕Нa XII, 7 seq.). ↩︎

  4. 129:2 Prof. R. Wallace’s ‘India in 1887’ (plate 39) contains a photographic representation of an Indian goat with pendicles like teats. ↩︎

  5. 129:3 In the case of the ‘som─Бtipavita,’ not the ‘somav─Бmin,’ the Taittir─лyas slaughter a fourth victim to Br╠еhaspati. ↩︎

  6. 130:1 This portion of the legend is but a repetition from I, 6, 3, 1 seq. A few alterations are, however, made here in the translation. ↩︎

  7. 130:2 Or, ‘Soma from which Indra was excluded’ (apendra), as formerly translated; a closer rendering of the succeeding clause making this change desirable;–even as Indra was excluded from the Soma-juice when produced, so he remained excluded from it (when it was offered up). ↩︎

  25. 135:1 That is, over the southern one of the two new fires, the one laid down on a raised mound. ↩︎

  26. 136:1 These triplets to the Fathers are given V─Бj. S. XIX, 49-51; 55-57; 58-60.–The Taitt. ritual here has a curious variation. After the remainder of the (pure) liquor has been offered to the Fathers, a Br─Бhman is to be bought over to drink the dregs; and if such an one cannot be found (willing to do it), they are to be poured away on an ant-hill. This is to be done for the sake of atonement. ↩︎

  27. 136:2 That is, according to K─Бty─Бyana (XV, 10, 19) and S─Бyaс╣Зa, the pa┼Ыu-puroс╕Н─Б┼Ыa, or cakes of the animal offering. The performance of these is irregular, inasmuch as their deities are not the same as those of the animal sacrifice (the A┼Ыvins, Sarasvat─л, and Indra Sutr─Бman). Taitt. Br. I, 8, 6, 1, however, explains that in this case the animal sacrifices are without ‘animal cakes,’ the libations of liquor, which indeed are offered to the same deities, being in lieu of them. ↩︎
